## Analysis of Response A  Response A is a Python program that uses a generator to find the common elements in two arrays without using any extra data structures. The program uses two pointers, i and j, to traverse the two arrays. It checks three conditions at each step:  1. If nums1[i] == nums2[j], then it yields the common element and increments both pointers. 2. If nums1[i] < nums2[j], then it increments i since the current element in nums1 won't be common. 3. If nums1[i] > nums2[j], then it increments j since the current element in nums2 won't be common.  This continues until one of the arrays is exhausted. The function uses a generator to yield the common elements without storing them in any extra data structure.  ## Analysis of Response B  Response B is a Python program that finds the common elements in two arrays without using any extra data structures. ## Analysis of Response A  Response A implements a function `findMedian` to find the median of two sorted arrays. The function uses a divide and conquer approach to find the kth smallest number in the combined array, where k is the total length of the two arrays divided by 2. The function recursively divides the problem in half, finding the kth/2 smallest number in one half and kth/2 smallest number in the other half. The base cases are when one array is empty (just take from the other array) or k = 1 (just take the min of the first elements). The function runs in O(n) time since it does a single pass of each array, and O(1) space since it does not use any extra space in the recursion.  ## Analysis of Response B  Response B implements a function `find_median` to find the median of two sorted arrays. The function uses a binary search approach to partition the two arrays such that the left half of the combined array contains elements that are smaller than the right half. The function calculates the median based on the maximum element in the left half and the minimum element in the right half. The time complexity of this algorithm is O(n) because it only needs to perform binary search on the smaller array, and the space complexity is O(1) because it only uses a constant amount of extra space to store variables.  ## Checklist Evaluation  Based on the checklist, here is the evaluation of Response A and Response B:  1.
